Enticement Followed by Tolerance: The Untamed Nature of a Live-in Son-in-Law 160

Expelled Before Engagement

Accused Again of Enticement

Xu Jinsheng of Yuyao, residing at No. 20 Xinhe Lane, Yishan Road, has a daughter named Fengmei, currently only nineteen years old. Two years ago, when the Xu family lived at Qidaitou, Longjiang Road, Fengmei was only seventeen and still a young, unmarried girl. Their neighbor, Hu Yougen, was ten years older than Fengmei and did not engage in proper work, thus remaining unmarried. He frequently used suggestive language towards Fengmei, arbitrarily enticing her. Around the Lunar New Year of last year, Hu suddenly took the girl to the Great World amusement park one evening, and they did not return home together. Instead, they went to a small inn on Guangdong Road for a night of passion. From then on, the girl was repeatedly defiled, but fearing her father's reprimand, she kept it a secret. It wasn't until May that Xu Jinsheng discovered the truth. He confronted Hu, whose father and elder brothers argued that since the deed was done, publicizing it would damage both their reputations. Fortunately, one was yet to marry, and the other was waiting to be betrothed. They could marry promptly to form a family, fulfilling their mutual desires and saving face for both sides. They persuaded Xu to set aside his resentment and embrace the union. Xu, left with no choice, reluctantly agreed and urged the Hu family to quickly hire a matchmaker for an early engagement. However, Hu Yougen requested that Xu allow him to live with the daughter at her parental home as if he were marrying into the family. Xu couldn't bear to refuse, so Fengmei and Hu appeared to be a formal couple. Hu then took further steps, interfering in Xu's household affairs and constantly demanding money from Fengmei for his own extravagance. The girl, who worked at a sock factory, had her savings entirely depleted. On June 13th of this year, Fengmei gave birth to a daughter. Hu not only showed no affection but grew increasingly disgusted with his unmarried wife, neglecting the marriage arrangements. The Xu family, father and daughter, deeply resented the cuckoo's occupation of their nest and felt that Hu's temperament was violent and increasingly depraved, associating only with idlers. The outcome would inevitably be dire. Fortunately, they had not formally engaged, making it easy to banish him from their home. Therefore, they issued a strict order for him to leave and hired a lawyer to sue Hu in the First Special District Local Court for enticing a minor, seeking punishment according to Article 257, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan held a hearing. Due to the case's content being related to public morals, the court had to prohibit spectators. Judge Zhan dismissed all spectators from the courtroom before questioning both parties individually. The result was that he advised both parties to attempt reconciliation outside of court. If reconciliation failed, a continued hearing would be scheduled.

Municipal Guoshu (National Martial Arts) Hall Welcomes Guoshu Expert Zhang Xuebin 161

Mr. Zhang Xuebin is from Sichuan. From a young age, he was taught by extraordinary individuals, learning Guoshu techniques deep in remote mountains and valleys. After more than ten years of rigorous training, he mastered both soft and hard skills, especially the unique feat of setting up a Lei Tai (fighting platform) on Plum Blossom Poles. This time, he has come to Shanghai at the invitation of old friends and various organizations to demonstrate his Plum Blossom Pole skills and set up a Lei Tai to find like-minded individuals, adding a special touch to the Guoshu community.

Yesterday, the local Guoshu Hall held a meeting to welcome Mr. Zhang. At 3 p.m., when Mr. Zhang arrived at the Guoshu Hall, the teachers and students had already gathered to welcome him. They exchanged greetings and expressions of admiration. After tea and refreshments, they were led to the Guoshu training ground behind the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. First, the students of the hall performed the Five Elements Sword, Broadsword, and Boxing techniques. Then, Mr. Tong Zhongyi, director of the Shaolin School, performed the Eight Immortals Sword and Double Halberds, with agile movements and steady techniques, demonstrating deep skill. Others, such as Instructor Jin Yunting with Xingyi Bagua, Instructor Zhao Shouchun with Taijiquan, Instructor Ma Wanlong with Shaolin Boxing, Instructor Liu Yunxiang with Shaolin Wrestling, Instructor Wang Zhenzhang with Shaolin Wrestling, Instructor Ma Hanzhang with Shaolin Boxing, and Instructor Yang Xiaowen with Taijiquan, were as nimble as monkeys and as fierce as angry tigers, balancing strength and gentleness, each with unique skills and dazzling performances, exciting the audience. After the Guoshu Hall's teachers and students finished their performances, Mr. Zhang was invited to continue with his first demonstration, the Luohan Fist. According to experts, this fist is not just any Shaolin technique. One must have deep understanding and exquisite skill to master it. When he gathered his Qi, his joints audibly cracked. From beginning to end, his hands and feet worked together, his movements swift and powerful. The second demonstration was the Double Sabers, named "Fierce Tiger Descending the Mountain." He placed the double sabers on the ground, leaped forward, supported by hands, raised both legs to form a 30-degree angle, and then flipped over, suddenly leaping up. Without lightness techniques, it would be impossible to achieve this. Afterward, the double sabers moved up and down with such fierce energy that only the blade light was visible, flashing incessantly. The audience was amazed. The third demonstration was the Single Saber, named "Eight Realities Saber." As it rotated, the blade created a sound like a tiger's roar. It was stopped short for fear the bending blade might break and injure the viewers. A complete show would have been preferred. The fourth demonstration was an internal Qi circulation technique. When he gathered his Qi, his body became like iron and stone, unharmed even by sharp knives or spears. He could even channel the Qi into others. After receiving this Qi, people who normally could not lift a chicken suddenly became impervious to knives and spears. This was proven on the spot and was not an exaggeration. Those present almost believed a deity had descended. To attain this internal Qi circulation, one must master both the Golden Bell Cover and Iron Shirt techniques to become as hard as iron and stone. Normally, the Qi is passed through the mouth. Mr. Zhang was able to channel it through his palm and transfer it to others, seemingly taking his mastery beyond the two advanced arts of iron and gold, an unbelievable skill that amazed everyone. After the performances, they returned to the hall. It was already 6 p.m. The guests and host shook hands and parted. Mr. Zhang's performance of the Plum Blossom Poles and Lei Tai in the Great World amusement park is drawing near. At that time, people in Shanghai will surely see something they have never seen before and be greatly entertained. Haig Road will be bustling with activity.

Advocating for Generous Compensation for the Deceased and Strict Punishment for the Culprit

The Remains Were Placed in a Coffin Yesterday at the China Funeral Home

Wu Yongmei, a female student from the Education Department of National Jinda University in Zhenru, was hit by a car with fellow students Hua Shuxian and Ouyang Shuxing on the 20th of this month while passing in front of the school. She was rushed to Southeast Hospital, but the doctor said her injuries were too severe to be saved. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. Her remains were placed in a coffin at the China Funeral Home at 10 a.m. yesterday. The two injured women, Ouyang and others, are out of danger. Details are as follows:

Organizing a Support Association The students of the school, deeply saddened by the female student's excellent character and academic performance, as well as her amiable personality, whether they knew her or not, specially formed the Wu Case Support Association, advocating for generous compensation for the deceased, strict punishment for the culprit, and the erection of a stone monument for permanent remembrance. The details of the female student's death have been telegraphed to her family and a request made for someone to come to Shanghai to take care of matters. A reply has not yet been received. According to information gathered by reporters from the Guowen News Agency yesterday, the female student's biological parents are both deceased, and only a stepmother remains, with whom her relationship was not very harmonious. Her being alone and orphaned is truly tragic.

Out of Danger The two female students, Ouyang Shuxian and Hua Shuxian, who were hit at the same time as the female student, suffered head injuries. Fortunately, they were not serious. They were taken to Southeast Hospital and, after careful treatment by the hospital's doctors, are now out of danger. They will be discharged from the hospital after half a month of rest. Their families and the teachers and students of Jinda University have been visiting them for days, but the two women sometimes feel dizzy, and too much conversation is detrimental to their injuries, so the doctors have generally refused visitors. The culprit, Lan Fuming, who caused the accident, was originally an expelled student from Jinda University. He was returning to Shanghai from his honeymoon in Nanyang, driving his own car, and accidentally caused the accident. He is still being held in the Local Court. It is reported that the Jinda University authorities will file a lawsuit with the court in the coming days.

Sun Fuxian's Discussion on Improving Tea Production 163

The China National Products Maintenance Association recently received a statement from member Sun Fuxian, claiming that our country's tea has long been famous and popular throughout the world. The six counties under the jurisdiction of Huizhou in Anhui Province, as well as Lu'an and Huoqiu counties, are famous for tea production. The livelihoods of the farmers in these counties depend on it, which is of great importance to our country's economic foundation. The tea produced in Taiping County, which belongs to the former Ningguo Prefecture, has the best aroma. According to the tea price ratio of each county, the annual output value of the county is about 2 million yuan. However, tea farmers stick to old methods and do not know how to improve. Moreover, due to inconvenient transportation, it is only sold along the Yangtze River, not exported, resulting in oversupply and blocked sales, causing farmers and merchants to suffer, and rural bankruptcy, which is regrettable. In addition, this year, the county suffered a severe drought, and food is scarce, which has caused panic. Fortunately, the Yintun Highway has been built to Taiping, and more than 10,000 farmers have gone to work and find food, which can temporarily save the current situation. However, winter is approaching, and the farmers in the countryside who have no clothes or food, how can they bear it? I have always had the ambition to improve Taiping tea and increase production to benefit the countryside. Now, tea merchants from the county have sent representatives to contact various places and petition the government to find ways to rescue them, and to request that farmers' banks and other banks set up branches in Taiping to help tea farmers and maintain production. (The completion of the Yintun Highway will allow Taiping tea to be transported directly to Shanghai via Tunxi for export) to consolidate the foundation of the rural base, etc. Comrade Sun has deep experience in the tea business and is currently the Shanghai business director of the Chizhou Baolong Coal Mine Company. In addition to the above tasks, he also plans to promote the sales of white coal from the mine. After the coal samples arrive in Shanghai, they will be sent to the association and distributed to major factories for trial combustion.

Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association Preparatory Committee Holds Talk Meeting with All District Land Guards 170

The Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association held a land guard talk meeting at 2 p.m. on September 21st at the Gaoqiao Town Fire Brigade Auditorium. Attendees included Wang Daquan, Huang Jincai, Shen Guanlin, Wang Jinshan, Zhou Jingui, Huang Guilin, Chuan Zhangqing, Gao Guiquan, Xu Jingren, Qu Xiangtao, Chen Shunyuan, Zhong Youliang (Mr. Lu on behalf). Special guests included Zhong Yuliang, Ding Rusong, Yin Yucun, and Zhang Bingrui. The meeting was chaired by Director-General Wang Kuiheng and recorded by Zhong Tianshi. First, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting: "Today, we have invited you for two reasons. First, we are the staff of the Rural Improvement Association and should first understand the situation in the countryside. The entire rural area of ​​the district is very wide, and it is not easy to know everything at once. Therefore, we invite you to tell us about the situation in your respective districts. Second, the management of rural improvement cannot be successful by only a few people, so we need a lot of help from the landlords. Now we must first recognize and connect emotions. As for the affairs of rural improvement, there are thousands of threads, but only one can be done at a time. The most needed thing at present is to increase the income of farmers, so that a boat of idle youths who do not do their jobs can be gathered together and receive training in relevant production skills. On the one hand, they can find a way out for their own future, and on the other hand, they will not harm the local area. There are also children in the countryside who cannot attend school due to various reasons. We should also think of ways to give them the opportunity to be educated. Finally, there is one point that I must make clear to you, that is, this association is not a government office. All events are hoped to be resolved through peaceful and persuasive methods, mutual cooperation, and absolutely no nature of coercion or oppression. A district-wide survey will be conducted recently, and I hope you will explain it to the public in detail to avoid misunderstandings." Next, Mr. Zhong Yuliang, a member of the municipal government of the district and a director of the association, gave a speech, roughly saying that the Rural Improvement Association was founded by Mr. Du Yuesheng of this town with his own funds. Mr. Du is seeking happiness for his hometown, and you should also be enthusiastic and helpful. Only by solving the difficulties of farmers will we not solicit a single penny or cent of donations from the local area. This point must be explained to the public and vigorously promoted. Then, Mr. Yin Yucun, a respected person in the area, gave a speech, roughly saying that the Rural Improvement Association is not being held elsewhere, but is being held in Gaoqiao. This is really the happiness and honor of the Gaoqiao people. Several gentlemen in the association are mostly outsiders and are not familiar with the local situation. In order to avoid gaps in doing things, we have specially invited you to tell us about the situation in your respective districts today. At the same time, we will need your help in the future. I hope that Gaoqiao will be well managed and then promoted to various places, so that the country will naturally become strong. There is one more point. Smoking and gambling are great harms to the country. The government has failed to prohibit them for many years, and they are very popular in rural areas. I hope the Improvement Association will find appropriate methods to help the administrative authorities in banning them. After the speech, the chairman asked everyone to report on the number of households in the villages under their jurisdiction and their locations. The staff of the office then prepared wontons, and they talked and ate, ending in a joyous departure. The meeting ended at half past four.

The Marvel of Flea Circus 171

Directed by Dong Shoujing from Zhejiang

Performed at the Great World

Mr. Dong Shoujing from Zhejiang spent his entire life training fleas to perform circus acts. He traveled around various countries and was highly praised by foreigners. Although a small skill, it is truly a spectacle. Mr. Dong can speak fluent English and humorous Mandarin, manipulating tiny insects in his palm. The equipment is also very scientific. Under a microscope, one can see the fleas performing various tricks, such as pulling a cart weighing two thousand times their own weight, kicking a ball weighing five times their own weight, jumping through colorful clothes, dragging a wheel weighing five thousand times their own weight, and incredibly agile hoop jumping. The performances are skilled and the movements are agile. They are now performing at the Great World. Those in Shanghai who want to feast their eyes can go and see it.

Reading Q&A

On the Theme of Creation 177

| Reply to Wu Li Jun |

(What should I write?)

According to Mr. Hu's letter, whenever he picks up a pen, he always asks himself this question and feels like there is nothing to write.

This is a matter of the theme of creation. All beginners in writing will encounter such difficulties: sometimes there are a thousand and one things, but no way to start, because they don't know how to choose and organize the theme of creation; sometimes, the belly is empty, there is nothing to write, also because they don't know how to recognize the theme of creation. Once the theme problem is solved, the situation of a "frozen pen" will naturally disappear.

What is the theme of creation? Simply put, the theme is the backbone of the article. For a house, the beams are the theme of the house. In literary terms, the theme is the reality expressed in the work, the central issue depicted. There is a difference between theme and material (subject matter). Various phenomena in society, when they have not happened in relation to the author, existing objectively and independently, are called subject matter. Once they are subjectively selected, organized, and written into a work by the author, then it is not a simple subject matter but a theme. For example, a drought. The objective fact of a drought, we can only say that it is a great subject matter for current creation, because when it exists independently before being recognized by the author, it is only a phenomenon, and it is unknown whether it will be written into a work by the author. However, once recognized by the author, written into a work, and organized into a systematic story, exposing its reality as much as possible, then the drought becomes the theme of that work. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Recording Proverbs 178

— Chen Zizhan

In various local dialects, I think the most wonderful parts are the four types of: nursery rhymes, proverbs, riddles, and puns. Nursery rhymes include children's songs, proverbs and riddles need no explanation, and puns include tongue twisters and drinking games.

For now, let's just take proverbs as an example.

Proverbs are aphorisms in spoken language, and are often used as maxims in spoken language. Guo Shaoyu said in (A Study of Proverbs):

A proverb is the result of a person's practical experience, expressed in beautiful words, which can be used openly in daily conversation, and is a formula for regulating human behavior.

Mr. Guo's definition of proverb is very correct. In modern times, the study of proverbs seems to have started with him; the recording of proverbs, as individual pamphlets, I have only seen Ye Dejun's Collection of Huai'an Proverbs.

Mr. Ye's collection of proverbs is a very thin book, with 275 proverbs, 44 agricultural proverbs, and 200 tongue twisters. Of course, the author's attention is limited to one township and one county, and the individual's listening is limited, and what he can remember is also limited. It is already very difficult to achieve such results.

I remember when I first entered middle school, I saw a book called "Yi Fa Tong" (One Method Through), the author was Wu Xie from Linxiang. Speaking of Wu Xie, he was a famous person in Hunan, he was an old celebrity. It is said that when Division Commander Wu Ziyu was stationed in Yuezhou, he knew that this old celebrity was very poor, and gave him several hundred yuan. I don't know if it was the division commander's subordinates, or the straggling northern soldiers, who heard that the old celebrity actually had a large sum of money one day, went to his home to (initiate), scaring the old celebrity who was over seventy years old to death. Now, what makes a few people in Hunan remember this old celebrity is the book called "Yi Fa Tong".

What kind of book is "Yi Fa Tong" written by Mr. Wu Fengsun?

I have read this book, it has two volumes, upper and lower. The author arranges the ancient and modern proverbs according to the order of the poetic rhymes, starting from three-character phrases, and ending with many phrases, similar to the form of (Sound and Rhythm Enlightenment). Therefore, the book is named (Yi Fa Tong), because the first chapter is in the "Dong" rhyme, and the first sentence is (One method through, all methods through). This book is very popular in the area around Yueyang Linxiang, the hometown of Mr. Wu. I think it can still be bought now. This is a work that has contributed to folklore studies since Yang Shen's Ancient and Modern Proverbs, etc. It is a pity that I don't have this book on hand now, so I can't give a detailed introduction. If someone can buy this book for me, I would be overjoyed!

In the eighth volume of Zhu Mu Xiang's Mingzhai Xiaoshi of the Qing Dynasty, there is a (Wu Xia Proverbs Couplet) entry, saying that Wang Guan, a commoner of the state of Wu, had many feelings, and later in his old age, he compiled four volumes of Wu Xia Proverbs Couplets, many of which are well-made and clever. Five-character phrases such as | | |

Catching lice on a tiger's head, gold-plated stone eggs,

Digging loach out of a cat's mouth. Blackened paper lantern.

Zhong Kui catching little ghosts, god of the latrine before the pit,

Luo Han inviting Amitabha. Local gentry on the platform.

Eyes hungry, stomach empty, heating loach in a pen tube,

Tough mouth, brittle bones. Feeling for clams under the bed.

Hot air replacing cold air, eyes red and hopeful,

Big insects bullying small insects. White intestines.

Seven-character phrases such as | |

Burdening the neighbors to eat thin porridge,

Instigating the master to heat the casserole.

Threading somersaults through copper coin eyes,

Performing rituals in a snail shell.

Sheep go to eat grass, geese go to chase,

Chickens come to collect debts, ducks worry.

East hand receiving money, west hand sending it away,

South sky raining, north sky clear.

Female chickens, male ducks, short head cloth,

Sharp knife, hot water, dry towel.

Eight-character and ten-character phrases such as | |

Little children eat radishes, peeling them piece by piece;

Monks have no hair, happy to shave.

Mothers want to marry, the sky wants to rain,

The rich don't teach, the poor don't study.

Adopting a daughter-in-law, employing a matchmaker, is also difficult to guarantee;

Old monks watching dog fights, I am not as good as him.

Nine-character phrases such as | |

Old gods of longevity eating arsenic, tired of living;

King Yama opening a restaurant, ghosts don't come.

Only caring about sheep's testicles, not caring about sheep's life;

Only seeing sheep drinking water, not seeing sheep urinating.

This Wu Xia Proverbs Couplet, although well-organized and clever, I think it is inevitable that the original words of the proverbs are changed to suit the antithetical parts. Compiling up to four volumes, one cannot but admire his willingness to spend so much effort, although he only sees it as a game, a pastime. But I don't know if this book has a printed edition? If there is no printed edition, I don't know if his descendants or other bibliophiles have a manuscript? This is a very useful book in folklore studies, which can be combined with Wu Xie's Yi Fa Tong and printed together.

Some people say that there are too few vocabularies in vernacular Chinese, and the diction is not enough. You have to find it in books such as Literary Selections, etc. Everyone knows that this is unnecessary.

In reality, if we are willing to write articles in a spoken and written language that is close to the public, apart from the need to use foreign words and newly created words, sometimes we must also borrow a few simple words, and try to find vocabularies and diction from the living languages ​​popular in the folk, which is even more necessary. Therefore, I hope that people from all over the world can spare a little time and put in a little effort to record the proverbs of their hometowns in the best way they think possible. This is also part of our practice of material work.

Impressions of Changsha 179

— Lin San

The people of Changsha are capable of anything. For example, if a woman walks down the street without socks or with her chest exposed, many idle people will scold her as a "witch," "foreign woman," or "traitor." If they are more serious, they will even throw stones at her. If a young couple walks side by side (note that you absolutely cannot find Chinese men and women walking arm-in-arm in Changsha), everyone will focus their attention on them, make faces to shame them, and a large group of idlers will follow behind, scolding: "Shameless ugly things!" "Ugly ghosts!" "Where did these monsters come from!"

A classmate and her husband had just returned from France. Because they didn't have Chinese clothes, they wore Western suits and high heels when they walked on the street. As a result, they were scolded so much that she barely dared to go out and hurriedly bought cloth to rush to make cheongsams. I asked her, "Have you been hit by stones?" "Fortunately, I haven't been hit yet, but I've been scolded enough!" she said, shaking her head as if she couldn't believe that such a phenomenon would occur in a traditionally civilized Changsha.

In fact, they can only show off in Changsha. If they go to Shanghai, Hankou, or Hong Kong, there are "witches" everywhere, and they can't be scolded enough. (To be continued)

Diversity in Unity 180

— TK

Village Chief (10) 181

— Wang Renshu

"It's that guy who conscripted soldiers!" Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, pretended to be experienced. It seemed like he had been reading this notice all night.

"Wasn't it posted a few days ago? Damn it!" Da Jiao Feng Muren sat on the wooden crossbar of the Cuizhu Pavilion, continuing.

"It was posted, but it was torn down! I don't know what turtle bastard did it!" Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, rarely used this rather classist curse (son of a bitch), but recently he has been in contact with the people in the yamen more and more, so he has learned a little. But he also added the local curse (turtle), omitting the word "egg".

"Tear it!" A young farmer, Daogou, shouted loudly. "What's the use of tearing it down? Who would do this dirty business?"

"Hmph! See if you don't go! See if you, Daogou, can hold out!" Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, stretched out his ginger-joint-like hand, pointing at Daogou. "Seventy-two conscripts in the whole village! The register has been prepared, with names on it. See if you don't go! See if you don't go!"

Shoufu Aidaibao watched from the side, stuck out his tongue, said "Heh!" and turned around, squatting on the stone platform at the entrance of the pavilion, holding his head.

"I didn't tell you to go!" Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, was quite eloquent, first clearing himself of any responsibility, and then he said a lot: "If you don't go, I'm even happier. Do we lack a big cannon like you in our village? But, I'm afraid things won't be so easy. The words from above have already been spoken, and we have to do it. Since we have to do it, those with names will have to go."

"Hmph!" Kaiyang Mapizi didn't believe it. "What's the use of opening the list of names? We don't have words carved on our foreheads! As long as the people in the village keep their mouths shut and don't say who is who, see who he calls to go."

This reasoning was valid, and everyone in the entire pavilion laughed "Hehe!". Several rays of light immediately appeared on their faces.

Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, seemed to be stumped. He had nothing to say. Then Daogou, the young man, cursed: "Only dogs bite people, whoever bites out who is a dog."

As he cursed, everyone's eyes swept to Dong Sheng, the lame-handed. Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, immediately understood that he was a village policeman. Damn it, being a village policeman is really not a job for humans! If I have a job, I will never do this shitty job!

Under the attack of all eyes, Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, to avoid it, looked through the pavilion and towards the street. He happened to see the sign outside Maolong Store.

"Hmph! Hmph!" Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, immediately raised his throat. "See if you don't go! See if you don't go! If no one says it, you still have to go. You just need to look at this thing." Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, raised the hand that wasn't lame, straightened his middle finger, and pointed towards Maolong Store. Standing outside Maolong Store at this moment was A Zhao, a (conscript). A Zhao saw Dong Sheng, the lame-handed, pointing at him, and thought something was wrong, so he walked over. Looking at A Zhao's dejected appearance, it seemed that he had had a fight with someone.

Wonders of the Deep Sea 182

— Special

Of the parts of the earth with life, the seabed is the least known to people. Our knowledge of deep-sea life comes entirely from specimens of several kinds of fish, all of which were caught in nets after they died.

Dr. Pi Bai, director of the scientific research department of the New York Zoological Society, in order to explore knowledge of deep-sea life, used a new method of submersion many times in 1930 and 1932. With the technical assistance of Barton, he made a two-ton steel ball. This ball is airtight on all sides and equipped with small windows made of fused silica, through which you can see everything in the water. He and Barton sat in the ball and submerged in the deep sea outside Bermuda (between the West Indies and Newfoundland) nearly twenty times, reaching a depth of 2,200 feet, which is the deepest point in the sea reached by living people. This summer, he received a large donation from the National Geographic Society of Washington and will continue his observation of deep-sea life.

Each time they submerged, a large cargo ship first carried the steel ball to the vast ocean, and then slowly lowered the ball. Inside the ball was a powerful searchlight that constantly emitted white light, illuminating the strange depths of the ocean transparently. At this time, many bulb-shaped phosphorescent strange fish, attracted by the light, swam through the light like weaving shuttles. Dr. Pi Bai's face was close to the window, and he briefly narrated everything he saw to the telephone. On the deck of the cargo ship sat a stenographer, with a telephone receiver on his ear and a notebook in his hand, recording Dr. Pi Bai's words in shorthand.

The outer shell of the ball is made of 1.5-inch-thick fine steel, and inside are placed measuring instruments, thermometers, and other scientific instruments. It is also equipped with several oxygen tanks, because air cannot be drawn from the surface to the depth reached by the submersible. Each tank has an automatic mechanism that releases two liters of oxygen per minute. There are also two wire racks, one with calcium chloride, which is used to absorb moisture, and one with soda lime, which is used to remove excess carbon dioxide in the air. When the ball reaches the deep sea, the people in the ball rely on slightly high-pressure air to survive. This summer, several new windows made of fused silica, three inches wide and eight inches long, were installed. Fused silica is the strongest and most transparent material in the world, capable of resisting extremely high underwater pressure.

The ball has a small door for people to enter and exit, weighing 400 pounds. When entering the ball, you have to climb over the crossbar, which is very troublesome. Then lift the door, put it into the groove, tighten it with screws, and then tighten it with an iron hammer. The sound almost deafens the people in the ball. It is even more difficult when exiting the ball. Although Dr. Pi Bai is an experienced adventurer, he always looks pale when exiting the ball each time.

After everything is arranged properly, the ball is lifted from the deck with a powerful crane, moved to the side of the ship, and slowly lowered into the sea. The momentum of the ball and the length of time in the water are all directed by the telephone in the ball. Once the ball is parked at a certain depth, the people in the ball begin to observe.

As the ball descends to the bottom of the sea, the light in the water gradually decreases, and the water pressure gradually increases. In the blink of an eye, it passes through the pure blue floating fish layer and enters a semi-bright and semi-dark area, where everything can be seen. Descending further, it becomes as dark as ink, and the ball stops. At this time, it is half a mile deep from the surface of the sea. The water here is very cold, almost motionless, and the water pressure is extremely high, so the fish obtained from this depth often burst when they reach the surface of the water.

Dr. Pi Bai once said: "The deep blue that appears in the deepest part of this ocean is indescribable. It is completely different from everything I have seen in the upper world, and it confuses our optic nerves to the extreme. We think about it all the time, and we always call it brilliant. I picked up a book to read many times, but I only felt that there was no difference between blank pages and colored plates."

Dr. Pi Bai submerged many times and saw many fish with light-emitting and flashing organs. The eyes of these fish are very sharp and can swim freely in the dark. Dr. Pi Bai saw clusters of bright light moving slowly in the water in the ball. There were also some that jumped very fast. He used a searchlight to illuminate them and saw that they were all long, hatchetfish with glittering bodies. When they swam through the light of the searchlight, the light on their bodies disappeared, and when they came out of the light, they were bright again. Some of the fish were completely black, some were completely red, and the light came from their heads, gills, and tails. Some came from both sides of their bodies, like a ship with lights on in the dark night, with bright light shining out from the small round portholes on the side of the ship. The colors of the light were different, some were dark red, some were yellow, and some were light purple. Some glowed permanently, and some glowed intermittently, like the light advertisements in a theater. Once, Dr. Pi Bai used a searchlight to illuminate all around and found that there were many extremely small creatures in two areas, separated by a wide section, but there were very few in between.

In 1932, the doctor descended many times in shallow water, and the ball rose and fell among the coral reefs until the ball frame fell into deep water. Once, a sharp piece of coral rock was horizontal under the surface of the water, blocking the ball. Fortunately, the cargo ship above quickly reeled in the cable, otherwise the steel cable tied to the ball would be wrapped around the sharp coral rock, and it would suddenly break. Then, with a loud crash, the ball would fall into the sea like a hard-shelled fruit falling from a tree branch. Dr. Pi Bai's submersion can be called a great discovery in modern science. In the future, it may be possible to find out how the coral and fish in the water become the coral and fish in the middle layer of the water, and descending further, how the coral disappears and the fish become deep-water shapes. Oceanographers now know nothing about these changes, because the changing areas are uneven and cannot be netted, so there is no thorough method of inspection.

Sports News

Overseas Chinese Xu Chengji Retains the Java Tennis Championship 183

Defeats Japanese Oie Two to One

Runner-up in Doubles with Lin Xuyin

(Special Correspondent from Batavia) Mr. Xu Chengji, a tennis player representing our country at the Far Eastern Games in the Philippines this year, is an overseas Chinese from Java Island, Netherlands East Indies, in Southeast Asia. Mr. Xu has participated in many competitions in Beijing, Shanghai and other places in China. How his skills are, I think the compatriots in the motherland know very well, there is no need for the reporter to repeat it.

Beating Oie Xu returned from Shanghai and has been more active in tennis practice, and his progress has been quite rapid. At the beginning of this month, the Dutch Indian Tennis Association held the All-Java Championship in Bandung. Many Chinese people signed up to participate, and the situation was very lively. Xu Chengji won the championship in the competition last year, and of course he could not miss this opportunity this year, so he also participated. After several days of preliminary matches, Mr. Xu still overwhelmed the players. Yesterday (September 12th) was the final day. In the singles group, Mr. Xu and Japanese Oie competed for the final battle. Enemies meet, particularly clear-eyed. The intensity of this battle can be imagined. Therefore, even before the competition started, the tennis court was already full of spectators, especially overseas Chinese. However, Mr. Xu was unfortunately ill on that day, and the performance was not as brilliant as expected. However, the Japanese Oie was exceptionally stable. Except for the slightly weaker backhand, there were almost no flaws to attack. However, when the game reached ten to nine in the third set, Oie's strength began to fail, and his legs cramped, so he was forced to declare his abandonment. Therefore, the Java tennis championship this year was still won by Mr. Xu.

First Set As for the battle situation, the reporter originally intended to omit it, but in order to satisfy the general tennis fans in the motherland, I have to describe it below. It was found that the strategies of both sides on that day rarely used high lobs. Most of the balls they hit were both low and fast. Xu's smashes, volleys and drop shots, although in his physical discomfort, still did not lose the original color of the year. Cheers rose from the four seats from time to time. Xu's serve was not fierce this time, and Oie was generally able to hit it back. After the start of the second set, Xu immediately won a game, followed by Oie, creating a draw. Xu then took the lead with two to one. Oie also immediately caught up, and then pumped up his energy to win the first set with two to six. This was quite unexpected.

Second Set The first game of the second set still belonged to Mr. Xu, but the second game was won by Oie, and he continued to lose three levels in a row, creating an advantage of one to four. When Xu saw that the situation was about to collapse, he began to shake his arms and roll up his sleeves, and responded with determination, gaining an evenly matched situation. Unexpectedly, the ninth game was owned by Oie again, and there was a danger of being ended by him with four to six. Fortunately, Xu did not disappoint the expectations of the audience, and chased another game, making the score five to five. Then Mr. Xu used angled balls and backline shots, and finally won two games in a row, winning with seven to five. The frowning faces of the general audience were like wind sweeping away the clouds, gone in a roll.

Third Set After the third set continued, Mr. Xu began to gain the encouragement of the audience, and his spirit increased greatly. Under heavy pressure and light lobs, he took three games, and then Oie regained one game. Mr. Xu still had the upper hand, and the number of games rose from three to one, four to two, five to twenty. At this point, the general audience all believed that the final victory had been repeatedly promised to Mr. Xu, but the matter was completely wrong. Because Xu accidentally lost a ball, Oie's courage suddenly increased a hundredfold, and he finally created a draw of five to five. This is what makes people feel sorry for. However, after this, Xu always had the upper hand, and Oie did not show weakness, following closely step by step, until after the number of ten to nine games, Oie finally collapsed and was defeated.

As for the men's doubles, Xu Chengji and Lin Xuyin also participated, but they were defeated by Suma et al. and Shabu Yue, and only won the runner-up. (Published on September 13th)

Soviet Union Holds 887-Kilometer Long-Distance Run 188

En Route, 25 Rivers Must Be Swum

Medical Research Council Observes Athletes' Bodies

Researching the Impact of Long-Distance Running on the Human Body

(TASS Moscow Dispatch, August 25th) A team of Soviet athletes is holding an 887-kilometer long-distance race from Engels City in the Volga region to Moscow. They will run for a total of eleven days, with only ninety-six hours actually spent running. There are seven participants, aged between twenty-one and thirty-six. En route, they must swim across twenty-five rivers, including the Volga River, where they must swim six hundred meters. During the race, they maintain a speed of ten to fifteen kilometers per hour, running approximately ninety kilometers each day. After medical examination, it has been proven that their health has not been damaged. The Medical Research Council is currently observing their bodies to study the impact of long-distance running on the human body.

Registration for the China Football Association Closes at 5 PM Tonight 190

Registration for this year's China Football Association League began, and as of yesterday, more than ten teams have officially registered. Registration will close at 5 PM today. Teams that have not yet registered are urged to quickly submit a formal letter to the secretariat (located at the Xie Jin Association office inside Shen Garden on Yanping Road) to complete all membership procedures. Teams joining the league must have their own field. If borrowing a field, they must submit a certificate from the field owner approving the borrowing, as well as the address, length, and width of the field, the name of the person in charge, and contact information, etc., to the secretariat for verification. Joining the cup competition is not subject to this requirement. Teams that do not join this year's league or cup competition should also send a letter to notify us for record-keeping purposes.

Jiangnan University Sports Association Executive Committee Discusses This Year's Competitions 191

Fewer Than Three Schools Participating Will Not Be Considered a Championship

Methods Will Be Devised to Hold Current Games That Popularize General Sports

The Jiangnan Universities Sports Association held an executive committee meeting at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA on the morning of the day before yesterday (23rd). Representatives from six schools—Central, Jinling, Fudan, Chizhi, Guanghua, and Jinan—attended. Guanghua's Rong Qiguang, chairman, discussed the details of this year's competitions among the schools. Details are recorded as follows:

Important Resolutions Resolved: The following important resolutions were resolved at this executive committee meeting: (1) If three or more schools participate in a competition, it will be considered a championship. If fewer than three schools participate, it will be considered an exhibition. (2) The tennis competition venue is set for Nanjing Jinling, with the date after October 15th. (3) The all-around cross-country competition venue will be at Chizhi. (4) The number of competitions that each school's athletes can participate in per day will still be limited to four, with the all-around and track and field competitions combined as one item for calculation (previously, it was counted as two items). (5) The football competition date remains in November to December.

Popularizing Sports The executive committee also held an informal discussion on the widespread development of sports in the Jiangnan universities. The executive committee members believed that the Jiangnan University Sports Association should not only focus on competitions for athletes from each school but should also pay attention to the development of general sports. Therefore, it was decided that each Jiangnan University should select more than a hundred students to participate in track and field or other competitions, and the average score of each school would be calculated to determine the rankings. However, this matter has not yet been officially decided.

Member Withdrawal The association finally exchanged views on member withdrawals. The committee members all believed that the withdrawal of a member should be done through a formal letter from the president of the representative school and with proper procedures. The general meeting must permit the withdrawal. Any other form of withdrawal will not be considered official.

Germany vs. France International Track and Field Meet 193

Germany 95 Points, France 55 Points

(Havas Agency, 23rd, Marburg, Germany) Athletes from France and Germany held a track and field meet. As a result, Germany won with 95 points against France's 55 points. Germany won a total of eleven events: 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, javelin, shot put, pole vault, long jump, 110-meter hurdles, and 400-meter relay race. France only won the 1,500 meters, 5,000 meters, and discus throw.

Educational News

Minister of Education Wang Shijie Speaks on the Current State of Chinese Education (II) 194

However, in the past three or four years, the government has strictly carried out mergers and closures of universities that were poorly managed, and has imposed strict conditions for the establishment and re-establishment of new universities. The previous abuses of extravagance have been slightly corrected. As for emphasizing practical subjects, various measures have been established in recent years (such as limiting the ratio of enrollment in liberal arts and practical science subjects in various schools). As a result, the orientation of schools and students has greatly changed (when several universities conducted entrance exams this summer, the number of students applying for liberal arts subjects was far less than the number applying for practical science subjects). In addition, for the past two years, the funding for national universities has not been reduced, and the equipment and administrative discipline of universities have also improved. Therefore, in the current situation, schools above the national vocational level are indeed entering a normal track. The current problems are: first, expanding the equipment of various schools, especially the equipment in the field of practical science; second, increasing the number of excellent university teachers. Currently, most universities feel the lack of excellent teachers, and domestic universities are still unable to cultivate university teachers due to the lack of research institutes. Therefore, the current policy should continue the policy of studying abroad and select suitable universities to prepare for the establishment of research institutes. Third, ensuring the stability of funding for public schools and providing relief to private schools with excellent performance. In addition, in order to encourage young students to improve and improve the academic atmosphere, the examination and appointment system must be universally implemented. Otherwise, the results of the school will be disconnected from the future of the youth, the political atmosphere will not be easy to improve, and the academic atmosphere will not be easy to improve.

Second, the status of secondary education: In the current education system, secondary education includes three types of secondary schools, namely ordinary middle schools (junior high and senior high), normal schools, and vocational schools. Since the Republic of China, the progress of public and private secondary schools across the country can be seen from the following figures in terms of quantity:

(A) Number of Schools

Number of middle schools in the first year of the Republic of China: 373

Number of middle schools in the 20th year of the Republic of China: 1892 (increased five times)

Number of three types of schools, middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools: 3021

(B) Number of Students

Number of middle school students in the first year of the Republic of China: 52,100

Number of middle school students in the 20th year of the Republic of China: 403,134

(Approximately 8 times increase)

Number of middle school, normal school, and vocational school students: 537,757

(C) Amount of Funding

Amount of funding for middle schools in the first year of the Republic of China: 3,034,704 yuan

Amount of funding for middle schools in the 20th year of the Republic of China: 39,171,385 yuan

(13 times increase)

Amount of funding for middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools:

54,053,363

In terms of the content of secondary schools, there are indeed still many bad schools in various places, and the composition of such schools is particularly obvious in metropolitan areas with many schools. However, in the past three or four years, the curriculum standards of secondary schools have been set by the Ministry, and the levels of each school have a statutory standard. In addition, in the past two years, the middle school examination system has been universally enforced, and schools and students have gradually been unable to muddle through. The improvement of the school level of general middle schools in the future can be predicted. There are indeed many aspects of moral education in middle schools across the country that need to be improved, but the management of many middle schools is indeed perfect. The biggest weakness of secondary education at present is that the proportion of ordinary middle schools is particularly large, and the proportion of vocational schools is particularly small. According to statistics from the 20th year of the Republic of China, out of 3,000 secondary schools, ordinary middle schools accounted for more than 1,800 schools, normal schools accounted for more than 800 schools, and vocational schools only accounted for more than 200 schools. The total number of secondary school students is more than 500,000, of which vocational school students only account for about 40,000, less than one-tenth of the total number. How to correct this maldistribution is the biggest problem facing secondary education at present. In recent years, the Ministry of Education has instructed all provinces and cities to revise their budgets and redistribute secondary education funds in order to achieve a roughly equivalent state of funding for ordinary middle schools and vocational schools in all provinces and cities before the 26th year of the Republic of China.

In addition, in order to promote communication of border information and student practical training, it is planned to publish a monthly magazine, which requires an additional 100 yuan per month. In total, there is a monthly shortfall of about 300 yuan. Now, the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission has approved a monthly subsidy of 200 yuan starting from January of this year, which will be allocated from other subsidies. However, since this subsidy was not listed in the original plan, the auditing agencies will have no basis for the reimbursement of the class in the future. The Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission has submitted the case to the central government for approval. It was notified to the Auditing Department and the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission by the Executive Yuan yesterday.

The Central Book and Magazine Review Committee Works Tightly 207

(Shanghai News) Since its establishment in Shanghai, the Central Book and Magazine Review Committee has reviewed more than 500 kinds of magazines and books in four months. On average, each staff member reviews more than 100,000 words per day. The review procedures are exceptionally fast. Even for huge works, it takes no more than two days. Therefore, the publishing industry generally believes that the speed is unexpectedly fast, which provides a lot of convenience. As for the review standards of the committee, unless the words are absolutely and obviously unfavorable to the party and the government, they are asked to delete and change them. The rest are based on impartiality and impartiality, without any partiality. Therefore, in recent months, everything has been fine. In the past, the publishing industry was often subject to detention or prohibition after the publication of books due to the lack of a review agency. Since the establishment of the review committee, this kind of event has no longer occurred. It is heard from the central government that the committee has achieved excellent work results, and the publishing industry urgently needs this kind of organization. There are plans to increase the number of internal staff in order to facilitate the review work.

Page 15

Special Issue on Spring and Autumn Qiantang Tide Viewing

Haining Tide and Haining Disaster 217

— Duansheng

Tides are common to all oceans. Why do people go to Haining to watch the tide in groups, especially in special trains? It is precisely because the tide in Haining is different from the tide in general oceans and does have a value worth seeing. The tide comes from the East China Sea. Once it enters Haining, it rises like a silver wall, galloping like ten thousand horses, horizontally in a line, rolling and surging, overturning rivers and seas, worthy of the four characters "majestic, magnificent, strange, and frightening" without shame. Therefore, the Haining tide is unique in the world and famous at home and abroad. It is a must-see.

Since the tide in Haining is so powerful, the people who live in Haining often worry that the tide will cross the dike and flood into the interior, lamenting "its fish". Unexpectedly, this year's drought did not turn them into "fish in a dry rut". Is this really a great misfortune for the people of Haining?

I remember that among the three prefectures of Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou, the great drought in the modern era occurred once in the 19th year of Jiaqing, which was also the year of Jiaxu, exactly two cycles of the sixty-year cycle ago, just one hundred and twenty years ago, and the disaster was also very severe. Another time was the great drought in the 6th year of Xianfeng (Bingchen). It is said that there was yellow plum rain in that year, but the drought started in mid-June, and it has been seventy-nine years since then. Although there were other days when the "riverbed faced the sky", they were very brief. Unlike this year's drought, the heat has exceeded previous records, and the time has been three months long. As soon as the plum season arrived, the drought began, and the disaster reached the point where there was no harvest. Perhaps it is a strange disaster that has never occurred since Haining existed!

Misfortunes never come singly. Haining could barely make a living, but unexpectedly, the silk market has declined in the past two years. The silk cocoons, which Haining people consider the "three spring can equal one winter" lifeline, are as cheap as cotton, and few people care about them. How can the people of Haining not be poor?

Only in the past ten days or so have there been several heavy rains. There is finally water in the rivers, but it cannot save the already dead rice. Ladies and gentlemen! If you see the disasters of Haining approaching, you should also shed a tear of sympathy!

Where Does the Tide Come From? 218

— Yu

Looking at the tide from books, they all say that it enters Biezimen and starts to sound like thunder. Otherwise, this is just an old saying. Biezimen is where the Qiantang River is divided into three mouths by the mountains of Kanze. The waterway between the mountains of Kan and the villages of Wentang and Hezhuang is called Daze; the waterway between the mountains of Wentang and Hezhuang and the Zeshan is called Zhongxiaze; and the waterway between Zeshan and the Haining Dike is called Beidaze. As of now, the mountains of Kanze have long been silted up into land, connecting with the south bank, dozens of miles away from the sea. The so-called Biezimen has become a historical relic. (It can also be said that Beidaze still exists.) However, its location is west of Haining, around Lao Yancang. Watching the tide is all in Haining, already outside Biezimen. It is absurd to say that the great tide is caused by the annual surge of Biezimen. However, it may as well be said that Biezimen is the place where the Qiantang River enters the sea. The west of it is the river; the east of it is the sea. Therefore, when speaking of the river, Biezimen can be cited, just like the Sanjia Water outside Wusongkou.

Then where does the tide come from? The tide comes from the East China Sea. The tide from the East China Sea is no different from the tide in general oceans. It passes through Zhapu, sweeps across Haiyan and Ganpu, and heads west. One only sees the waves surging and the water rising, but there is no magnificent sight of a giant thunderous silver wall standing high. When it enters Jianshan Pass, one begins to see white waves surging, connecting into a line, standing tall like a silver wall, crossing the river to the west, sounding like thunder, and forming a world wonder. From this, it can be known that the occurrence of the sea tide occurs at Jianshan Pass.

Why does Jianshan Pass create such a great tide? It is because the estuary extends northeast, wide on the outside and narrow on the inside. The tide enters from the northeast, vast and mighty; unexpectedly, the waterway becomes narrower and narrower as it progresses. Since the tide is bound by the terrain, it cannot stretch freely. The tide that heads straight for the south bank is also stirred up and heads north, meeting at the mouth of Jianshan. Moreover, the mouth of Jianshan is full of reefs, and the Tasha Dike also lies horizontally in the middle of the sea. The tide is stirred left and right, and the force becomes thicker and the momentum increases, so it surges high like a wall, and rushes west across the sea. The area around Babu is the most magnificent. When it reaches Nanmen in Haining, the force slackens slightly, and the crest of the tide is not very neat. When it reaches the old Biezimen and other places, the crest of the tide gradually flattens and is no longer worth seeing.

The Qianlong Emperor and Haining 219

— Xinan

Regarding Emperor Gaozong of the Qing Dynasty, no matter north or south, there is a legend that he was "the son of Grand Secretary Chen of Haining", which has been around for a long time. What exactly happened, even if Emperor Gaozong were raised from the ground, he would not be willing to tell the truth. However, according to the elders, there seems to be some connection between Emperor Gaozong of the Qing Dynasty and the Chen family of Haining. Perhaps it is also a conjecture and rumor by later generations; however, there is also a lot of information that can be regarded as unofficial historical material. I will tell you all about it when I have the opportunity to use it for after-dinner conversation. At this moment, just talking about watching the tide, we will talk about Emperor Qianlong and Haining from the aspect of the tide.

When you go to the sea dike to watch the tide, you will see the majestic stone dike, stretching for dozens of miles, which is worth praising for its greatness. This sea dike is called the Fish Scale Dike. This dike can indeed be compared with the Fish Scale Register compiled by Emperor Taizu of the Ming Dynasty, which has the same name but different functions. One clarified the national land tax; the other protected the lives of the people of seven prefectures. How is this stone dike built? It is made of very long strips of stone, stacked horizontally and vertically, forming a stepped shape (like fish scales, hence the name). It is up to ten feet high. The strips of stone on the dike surface (i.e., where pedestrians walk) are then reinforced with iron ingots. The gaps between the stones are mostly filled with iron filings and smoothed to prevent erosion by the tide. At the bottom of the stone dike, wooden segments several feet long are hammered in to make it solid. Outside of it, a strip of stone about a foot wide is also built to ease the water flow, so as to strengthen the dike body. In places where the tide is urgent, two tiers of stone is constructed in order to protect the dike itself. Only with such a solid project can it resist the attack of the raging tide; however, the power of the tide is too great, and over time, it will still wash away a section of the stone dike. Therefore, in the Qing Dynasty, annual maintenance projects were highly valued.

Before the Qing Dynasty, Haining's dikes included both wooden dikes and stone dikes, but none of the stone dikes that have been preserved today existed. The current stone dike! The Fish Scale Dike was launched in the first year of Yongzheng. Shangshu Zhu Shi was sent to Jiangsu and Zhejiang to discuss the construction of the sea dike, and special attention was paid to the sea dike in Haining. When he left, Emperor Shizong of the Qing Dynasty instructed Zhu Shi, saying, "Your trip to survey the dike is also to repay your teacher's kindness and should be careful"! This is because Zhu Shi and the Chen family of Haining had the friendship of teacher and younger brother. In the eleventh year of Yongzheng, more than 1.8 million taels of silver were allocated to start construction. Afterwards, they were gradually built. In the twenty-seventh year of Qianlong, he made his third southern tour and went to Haining to inspect the sea dike. He ordered the annual repair of the wooden dike in Lao Yancang and added a stone weir to protect it. He also personally inspected the stone dam (Tasha Dike) between Jianshan and Tasha and changed it to a strip of stone dam. He then inspected the Fujian Navy from the Tide Viewing Tower. In the thirtieth year of Qianlong, he made his fourth southern tour and arrived in Hangzhou in February, ordering the construction of the Haining stone dike. In the forty-fifth year of Qianlong, he made his fifth southern tour and went to Haining in March to watch the tide. He visited Jianshan. He ordered that all the Fish Scale Stone Dikes that were thin be rebuilt. The 4,200 feet of wooden dikes that could be rebuilt into stone dikes were also surveyed and handled together. In the forty-ninth year of Qianlong, he made his sixth southern tour and visited Jianshan in Haining to inspect the dike project. Although the project was completed, there were still many uncoordinated places. He then built a stone dike to the Wulong Temple, allocated 5 million taels of silver from the Ministry of Revenue, and connected the various allowances issued earlier, limiting the construction in sections from east to west within five years. The Hu Haining Dike took more than 60 years from launch to completion and cost approximately 10 million taels of silver; based on current prices and labor costs, it is approximately ten times that of the time, which means that it would cost 100 million taels of silver to complete it now.

Picture of the Tragic Situation of the Haining Drought 220

— (Bingru)

Emperor Qianlong went to Jiangnan six times, and four of them, in addition to sightseeing, can be said to be for the sea dike of Haining. Some people think that during the Qianlong period, the Yellow River overflowed 20 times, but it was never heard that Gaozong personally inspected it. However, he personally inspected the dike of Haining four times and allocated huge sums of money (one of which was 5 million taels); moreover, when he arrived in Haining, he resided in the Anlan Enclosure of the Chen family, which further deepened people's surprise and astonishment. Why was Emperor Qianlong so close to Haining? The author has no way to verify it, so I will leave it for the next time!

Blessed Old Man 221

— Bao Chen

The news of the drought disaster from my hometown (Haining) does not seem to have hurt me in any way, because I have been a maritime resident for several years and have never been panicked about "water".

This time, for a small matter, I took the opportunity to return home and stayed for five days. During these five days, I drank water with "earthy breath and muddy taste" and heard news of farmers in a certain township and village robbing rice. After lunch, I ran to the street, which was deserted like the first day of the Lunar New Year. I couldn't find the police standing guard; it is said that there were originally fifty police officers in our town, and more than thirty were sent to the countryside 丨丨 to intimidate and capture those rice-robbing villagers 丨丨 so there were not enough positions to be assigned.

"Tea sheds are being set up again in Huangdao Lake (Note 1) to sell tea!" A familiar person said to me on the road.

"Oh, Huangdao Lake, selling tea." I heard this story from my grandmother more than ten years ago. That was the year Xianfeng six of the Qing Dynasty. My grandmother saw it with her own eyes. If she were still alive, she would have been one hundred and one years old. Huangdao Lake is only eight or nine miles away from my hometown, so I wanted to take this opportunity to take a look.

At noon on the fifth day of my return home, we actually arrived at Huangdao Lake. Ha, this is where the "lake" is, it's simply a sports field! There is a natural swimming pool in the middle of the field, which is probably the ruins of Huangdao Lake? The Changshuiyan Bridge with twenty-seven bridge gates is erected on this wide field, revealing a full look of naivety. She can only be paired with Yan Ziling's fishing platform now. (Note 2)

Sure enough, many tea sheds were set up on the wide field. We did not drink tea there. Seventy-nine years ago, my grandmother (she was a twenty-something girl at that time) had also drunk tea here, I thought.

"Sir, do you know Old Man Youfu? He is ninety-two years old this year. Only he has seen the tea sheds set up in Huangdao Lake for the second time!" The person who poured the boiled water said to me.

"I haven't seen him." I said, "Is there any way to find him to talk to him?"

"He is drinking tea in the tea shed next door! But he is deaf, so there is nothing to talk about."

"Never mind him, just ask him to come over."

Old Man Youfu relied on his light and healthy waist and legs and actually ran to our tea shed alone. I greeted him respectfully and asked him to sit down, but he just smiled. We were eating eggs, so I peeled an egg and handed it to him. He shook his hands and started speaking in the Haiyan dialect, "Sin! Sin! Our country eggs should be eaten by the city people." While he was talking, he loaded his dry smoke, seeming to indicate that he would never accept it, so I had to take the egg back and pour him a cup of tea.

Everyone was silent. Many people stood by and watched.

"Xianfeng Six." Old Man Youfu opened his mouth, "At that time, I was only fourteen years old. No, although I was young, I still remember clearly that tea shops were also open here. ...That Changshuiyan Bridge had not been built yet. ...I never thought I would see it again this year."

"Did the villagers come out to rob rice at that time too?" I asked him loudly.

There was no answer. He didn't hear.

"The emperor should exempt us from taxation this year. ...The villagers are very bitter!" He said to himself.

"Hey! Emperor! Old Man Youfu always says that." A young farmer stood by and said with a smile.

"If there was an emperor, in such a drought year, he would always think of a way for us villagers. Didn't Old Man Youfu say that 'Although the year of Xianfeng Six was barren, the villagers were not as bitter as they are now'?" An old woman with red eyes interjected.

Old Man Youfu saw that there were many people around him, so he stood up and left. He greeted us, seeming to say, "There are too many people here." My companion followed him, and walked all the way to the bottom of the Changshuiyan Bridge and took a photo of him. The companion came back and said happily, "This photo is of historical value!"

Old Man Youfu left, and the people in the community were still discussing. Some said, "Old Man Youfu is really blessed. His grandchildren are already several decades old." Some said, "That doesn't count as being blessed! He should have died early if he was really blessed. Isn't the situation in his family getting worse year by year? He used to catch fish here with a net himself, at such an age!"

I had no opinion on those gossips, so I proposed to go back.

Tomorrow, I went back to Shanghai again. I didn't bring anything back except a photo of Old Man Youfu.

(Note 1) Huangdao Lake was originally named Lutiao Lake. It is located in the southwest of Haiyan County, Zhejiang Province, bordering Haining County. The lake surface is very wide. There is the Changshuiyan Bridge above, which is one hundred and eighty steps long.

(Note 2) The ruins of Yan Ziling's Fishing Platform on Fuchun Mountain are high on the mountain, with no water underneath, which is just like the Changshuiyan Bridge we saw.

Haining Begs for Disaster Relief Announcement 222

The Nining area is unfortunate and has suffered continuous disasters. The silkworm silk industry has declined since ancient times, and people's lives are struggling. The rural areas are already on the verge of bankruptcy; tens of thousands of households in the entire county are living on gruel every day. Unexpectedly, this year's yellow plum season has been bitterly dry, and all the green grass has withered. Four months have passed, and sweet rain has not fallen. As a result, the fields are cracked, the rivers are completely dry, and drinking water is difficult, let alone irrigation. The disaster victims are everywhere, and the tragic situation is difficult to express. The suicide of entire families is already not uncommon; and the robbing of rice and eating together has spread very widely. Thieves are rising, and robbery is rampant. There is already a phenomenon of the weak being thrown into the ravines and the strong risking their lives. Looking at the disaster situation, we deeply feel compassion and speculation. We hope that people of benevolence in the country and gentlemen from our hometown will generously donate to charity so that we can quickly plan for disaster relief, save the victims from sinking into disaster, and eliminate the disaster. The merit is immeasurable. The Haining Drought Disaster Relief Association respectfully announces.

Therefore, the market was weak, and merchants were bidding as much as 5-6 yuan below the offered price, resulting in no transactions. Both sides are currently in disagreement. It is heard that there will be another discussion today. If there is a convergence of opinions, a deal may be reached, but sellers will inevitably suffer losses. The only question is how much the losses will be.
