Talking Points

Christ Was Not From Judea 240

— Qiong Sheng

The telegraph dispatch on the 19th reported that the National Socialist Catholic in Germany (加特立穆勒) spoke in Hanover, arguing that under National Socialism, there can only be one country, one nation, and one church. Protestantism (Christianity) and Catholicism must merge into one national church, and any resistance will be punished with exile. What is particularly interesting is that, in order to avoid contradicting their anti-Semitism, they explained that (Christ was not from Judea) and was the first to declare war on the Jews.

Here, we naturally do not want to argue about a question that only Jesus's parents would know. What is worth examining is what is the significance of Germany making Jesus's (origins unclear) in this way. In European history, international wars have been caused by disagreements over religious denominations. In order to avoid internal unity being affected by religious relations, especially when relations between Italy and Germany are strained over the Austrian issue, and after the Pope opposed Hitler's religious policies, one of the reasons Germany announced the merger of the Old and New Churches. Secondly, after the swastika flag has been flying in Germany for more than a year, Hitler's most moving slogans of abolishing the Treaty of Versailles and solving the economic crisis have become (long dreams with many problems). In order to divert the people's dissatisfaction, he has played many new tricks, and the church merger is one of these methods. This is the second point. Furthermore, saying that Jesus was not of Jewish origin is obviously like Zheng Xiaoxu using the Way of Kings to cover up his own treasonous behavior, forcibly pulling Confucius and forcing Jesus to find other parents, each as their own political weapon.

Prison Joy 241

— Old Blow

A friend's servant was arrested on suspicion of theft, but he was not guilty. Later, thanks to the righteousness of the real thief, he was not falsely accused. It was proven that he was not an accomplice, and he was not questioned about the matter. He was detained in prison for three weeks before being released.

According to the servant, although prison is not easy, it is not entirely a miserable situation. There are also considerable moments of happiness. Truly, there is a land of joy in prison, no need for reputation or instruction.

In prison, apart from the absolute inability to find a way to secretly smoke opium, there is still a way to think about cigarettes, but the price is very high because they are contraband. Approximately every ten "Beautiful Brand" cigarettes cost four mao (small coins). And cigarettes are one of the most welcomed items by fellow inmates. If any of the inmates buys them, the owner at most gets to smoke two or three of the ten cigarettes, and the rest are quickly divided among his fellow brothers.

And the ways to solicit cigarettes also come with several different faces. Some take on the face of an uncle to ask for them, while others use lamentations, and before even half of the lament is finished, the cigarette is snatched away by a fellow inmate from the side and placed in his own mouth. This situation is roughly based on the qualifications and personality of the fellow inmate to determine the method used.

If a fellow inmate is found to have money, it is certain that they will be squeezed by their fellow inmates to treat them to something. Although cigarettes, alcohol, and other items are prohibited in prison, ordinary food can be bought at will and is not prohibited. Sometimes, when squeezing money from someone who has it, they will ask him to treat them to meat, which is also a very common thing (because fish and meat are not more expensive than outside the prison). The cooks also know the situation well, so they cut the meat into very small pieces. But after it is cooked and sent to the prison gate, the general fellow brothers who are waiting at the prison gate are already like customers at a newly opened grocery store, crowding outside the iron gate. As soon as they see the meat coming in, those with chopsticks use chopsticks, those with hands use hands, and they all attack the meat together. In an instant, it is all gone. The owner, at most, gets to drink some soup or some side dishes. This situation is extremely amusing.

Also, if they see that you have money, someone will come to flatter you. If you are assigned to wash dishes or pour out spittoons or toilets, they will come forward to do the work for you. If they know that you have money at home, the fellow inmates will definitely say, "What's the use of money to him? Now is the last time for you to use money. Why don't you write a letter home to ask for it?" If you can't write a letter, we can write it for you. We can fulfill some obligations for you.

Fellow inmates also have a happy time, which is when they are assigned to pour out spittoons and toilets. Prison inmates cannot step beyond the prison gate on ordinary days. At this time, they can take advantage of being on public duty to go outside. Having been in prison for a long time, the chest feels stuffy. At this benefit, they do not realize that the sky is high and the air is fresh, and their minds are broadened, truly like the students in private schools in the past who faked drinking tea and faked urinating. As for the inmates in the flat hall, they also have a few minutes of walking time every day, but general exercise is not as good as the joy of emptying toilets and spittoons. These are mostly the joyful situations in prison.

Sometimes, it is also seen that in extremely serious situations, a certain prisoner is taken away for questioning. A moment later, several gunshots can be heard faintly. At this time, one cannot help but feel a little nervous and frightened, and they lose color looking at each other. If there are important criminals in prison, fellow inmates often use words that do not enter the ears to encourage each other. They generally say, "The case you committed is nothing serious. Even if there are any mishaps, everyone only dies once. You can say that you died with a cause. You can rest assured, there is no need to be afraid, no need to think about it."

The writer notes that this is truly a land of joy in prison, but their joy is finding happiness in suffering, a kind of boring happiness. Those who usually act lawlessly outside do not know to love themselves. Once they are imprisoned, they realize the preciousness of freedom, but it is already too late. Although there is a land of joy within, it is still best not to ask about it.

Watching a Fight 242

— Jin Ren

Looking at the rain outside the window, a feeling of depression arises in my heart. Across from me is the attic room in the back alley. They have also closed their windows, wanting to enjoy the "rain scene" for themselves. It seems that this background is too simple; it is even more out of the question to write a poem about the scenery.

But people who add fun come to embellish this lonely rain scene, and there is not just one. It's as if they were specially sent to this alley to give me entertainment. They are a pair of typical figures that we can often see on the road. Looking down from above, their silk sleeves are rolled up very high. Although they are both wearing soft, straw hats, their straight faces can still be seen [illegible character]

Page 19

Roughly speaking, in other words, it is that the angle of their straw hats is sharper than the usual way of wearing hats. I first discovered this pair of friends who add fun when I heard two "What the hell" kinds of Shanghai words. It is said that water transmits sound, so although the windows were closed, the sound was very loud and powerful. In this simple setting, finding two sons of "hell" [meaning curse words], I had to open the window to see what was going on. It's really strange. As soon as my head peeked out of the window, many people had already gathered at the back door of the house across the alley. Naturally, these two sons of "hell" were trapped in the core. If applied to the art of film, it is the so-called overhead shot; however, I feel very regretful that I cannot see their legs clearly, so although I have skillful photographic cultivation, I cannot think of taking a photo to keep as a souvenir.

It should be stated here that the sky continued to drizzle, but those two friends who add fun became even more excited, jumping and gesticulating in the crowd. Their "hells", "sisters", "ancestors", and even "ancestors" all joined the battle from their mouths. Their voices were also getting louder and louder, giving the impression that Heaven made me, why did you make me? But do not say that I am watching a fight in the clouds, I think that instead of waving their hands in the air, why not just punch him in the heart? If the other party lost his footing and fell to the ground, the audience (or me) would cheer: "Hero forever!" But this continued for at least ten minutes. My desk was already full of raindrops. Naturally, the achievements on the bodies of the friends who added fun and those spectators were quite considerable. The fight had not yet succeeded. Anxious spectators shouted sideways ("Fight! Fight!"). With this cheer, my spirits lifted. If one of these two friends was in front of me, hum, I would send him home with this punch. But this shake quickly returned to normal. The hands of the parties were still waving wildly in the air for a while. All the "hells" and "ancestors" were finally [shouting] "Please", "I'll fight you!" I don't know why I am so enthusiastic. When I heard "Fight", [again, my] chest straightened up ("or just for the sake of watching the fight"). I thought that this time it would definitely be four fists waving, two heads colliding, a hard-fought and inextricable battle, a fight to the death. That group of rain-soaked spectators made the surrounding area even smaller so that they could see more clearly. Although I was alone in the window, I was not afraid of the rain and poked out my head. My own hands seemed to be full of strength. Just at this critical moment, an older man pushed through the crowd and desperately pulled and tore, trying to dissuade this "fight" situation; but if he had not tried to persuade them, it would have been fine, but with the persuasion, the two men's fists swung like raindrops. That older man became their shield and arrow target, and he was so scared that he hurriedly broke out of the encirclement. Strangely enough, the two friends immediately stopped and walked out along a gap, saying, "Hum, look at the old man's power!" Until they were completely out of my sight, a spectator looked up and greeted me. I asked them what they were doing. He thought I had not seen this scene and replied earnestly, "Fighting!"

Ah Xiu 243

— Simon

As soon as the autumn wind began to blow, Ah Xiu fell ill.

The grass raincoat-constructed hut, over time, became dilapidated with holes here and there. Looking up, one could see the azure sky. And the autumn rains were especially heavy, lasting for several days in a row. Rainwater streamed down through the holes, flowing everywhere, every puddle on the ground becoming a pool of water, dripping incessantly, from morning till night.

Basking in the sun in summer, getting drenched in autumn rain, a family of three – Ah You, her husband, and a child not yet ten years old – lived in this dilapidated hut, enduring the long days.

The husband lost his job two months ago. Since then, he couldn't find work anywhere.

And autumn had arrived again. The chilly morning breeze made people anticipate the icy cold winter that would follow. Poor families all frowned. Winter clothes were all locked away in the pawnshop, and their livelihood was uncertain. What to do? Worried about the approaching winter days, worried about the meals for the family of three.

The weight of worry exceeded what a frail body could bear, so Ah Xiu fell ill. So this was no ordinary illness, but one caused by too much depression and too much worry, sinking into the boundless edges of depression and worry. She couldn't bear it, and her spirit weakened day by day.

The illness worsened with the increasing sense of depression, and she lay in bed all day, groaning hysterically. Ah Xiu had almost lost the strength to even support herself and move around.

The sound of groaning mixed with the sound of raindrops, creating a desolate harmony.

(The child circles the edge of the bed, repeatedly tugging at Ah Xiu's wrist, complaining of hunger, wanting to eat).

(Wait a little! Daddy will definitely bring something back for you when he returns).

(Go wait at the door, Daddy will be back soon).

The mother opened her lifeless eyes, like the eyes of a dead fish. She painfully looked at the child's face. She stretched out a withered, firewood-like hand and stroked the child's head. In a low voice, she coaxed the child, barely able to catch her breath. The child listened to her mother's words and rushed out the door to wait for her father.

Two strings of crystal-clear tears silently crawled down Ah Xiu's pale yellow cheeks, like snails.

In the afternoon, the father had gone to the factory with Yuan Er Sao, a female neighbor and friend of Ah Xiu, to ask for back wages. He had also asked Yuan Er Sao to request another leave of absence from the factory.

If she could get all of the half-month's back pay, the family of three could live a bit more comfortably for half a month. Besides this, Ah Xiu's only hope was that her body would recover quickly, so she could go back to work soon.

Because if she couldn't go to work, all three of them would go hungry.

Ah Xiu thought about this and that, becoming so tired that she felt sleepy. In a hazy feeling, she suddenly glimpsed Yuan Er Sao being chased and pushed down by someone against the wall outside the factory gate. She struggled for a long time but couldn't get up. Then, several large men emerged, and her husband was being held by the collar by two people, dragged and chased, she didn't know where they were pushing him to.

With a jolt, Ah Xiu woke up and rubbed her eyes. Her body was still lying on the hard wooden bed. It turned out that it had all been a nightmare. (To be continued)

Thoughts on Autumn 244

— Huiren

Rain, in the clear autumn morning, drifting in strands, looking like the plum rain of April, but the climate not as humid and stuffy as during the plum rain season. Although there was no wind blowing, it was already much cooler. The morning glories on the wall outside the window were in full bloom, and it seemed that the vines had climbed higher today than yesterday. The flowers, which were only two or three yesterday, had also increased a lot today, among the verdant leaves, setting off red, purple, and blue flowers, looking truly gentle and lovely. The sky hung high above the spire of the chapel, and no floating clouds could be found flying. Sometimes, one or several rays of sunlight pierced through the uniformly colored sky, filtered through the drizzle, and shone on the top of the chapel, but they didn't evoke much warmth, instead, there was a sense of strange bleakness. Except for the mournful chirping of autumn insects, almost everything around was in stillness.

The enthusiasm left over from the hot summer had completely disappeared at this time. Although the gloom of autumn made people feel a bit uncomfortable, it was already much more refreshing than the heartbreaking spring and the restless summer.

But, in fact, something detracted from the heroic autumn morning, and that was the sound of gunfire disrupting the quiet of the autumn morning. These rattling and popping sounds really made people feel a bit terrified. Listening to the sound of leather shoes running fast on the street, one knew that they were practicing street fighting.

Then I remembered a sentence that Shawpona once said, namely; "ＭytheＷayofuokihgistotellthetruthlfworld" My jokes are the truth of the world. (Translated by the author) Now I chew on this witty remark once, twice, three times, even ten or twenty times, but I still can't get anything out of it, and even want to seek an answer in the snow-white beard and spirited and mischievous eyes of old man Xiao, but in the end, I am still confused, not knowing the true meaning of this sentence.

From one autumn several years ago until now, the sharp artillery fire has never stopped, and the terrifying sound seems to still vaguely linger in our ears. We seem to remember this sudden stimulus very clearly, and no truth has been sought out in mockery.

According to another group of people, the truth can only be obtained under the power of artillery fire. Then how should old man Suo's sentence be explained? I scratch my head and use all my strength to seek this answer, but the result is still a disappointment. However, there must be truth, and there are so many billions of people in the world who are longing for it. They don't seem to need to seek the truth in mockery, because if that were the case, they would have starved before they could find the truth.

At this time, the bells in the chapel rang loudly, and the sound of gunfire had subsided. The autumn rain was still drifting in the air.

Smoke 245

— Xiaolin

Like a loner who sees a cigarette as his only companion. Taking it, going out for a stroll, as intimately as taking a lover. Cigarettes have now become an indispensable necessity in my daily life.

At first, I didn't smoke, and I didn't even want to smoke. Not only didn't I want to smoke, but I also despised people who smoked. What's the taste? I always thought it was either a low-level expression of chasing fashion or a pointless waste. You think, holding it in your mouth, it's both bitter and astringent. Why not use this money to buy rice, chocolate, or something like that? Chewing it would at least have the sweetness that cigarettes don't have. But everyone likes it, it's like that everywhere, even young ladies and young performers smoke as if they know what they're doing. They bite a cigarette in their mouths, draped in cigarette ash, looking quite imposing. The allure of cigarettes is really not small. I always couldn't stand it. When I saw people smoking, I felt disgusted, not just disgusted, but also quite annoyed. I always avoided them, and almost wanted to snatch the cigarette from the smoker's mouth. But the smokers were enjoying it. Sometimes I was inexplicably angry for a long time.

I used to hate cigarettes and smokers to this extent. But now, I have actually turned into a smoke fiend, and my addiction is probably greater than that of the average person. I don't even know how it happened. From morning to night, I have a cigarette in my mouth, whether sitting or standing. Sometimes it's almost to the point where I can skip eating, but I can't skip smoking. It's simply my second life.

After smoking, I deeply realize that cigarettes do have many functions and subtle sensations that words cannot describe. They are almost more necessary than food.

The inspiration, illusions, and intoxication that cigarettes can give me are endless.

In the quiet and silent late night, under the quiet and bright lamplight, a person smokes, one cigarette after another, puffing away, slowly blowing out the smoke, watching the layers of smoke, one smoke ring after another, white and hazy, curved, winding up, transforming into various beautiful shapes. Eventually, they dissipate. After a while, it happens again. With half-closed eyes, putting one's mind and body in a state of self-forgetfulness, like sleepwalking in a field of colored gauze, each layer of smoke carries a faint, light meditation, and carries even more comforting longings that make the soul comfortable, faintly, so that they cannot be touched.

And one no longer feels lonely. Once one starts smoking, it's as if there is an invisible figure accompanying one's mind and body, and the soul has blended with it in a leisurely manner.

When one is bored, one often forgets the boredom because of cigarettes. Grasping the pen, staring blankly for a long time, unable to write a single word, one smokes a cigarette, and literary thoughts or inspiration naturally float up. Cigarettes have thus become the solace of my spirit, the lover of my spirit.

The reason cannot be explained. Even if it can be explained, it's still better not to. Leaving a bit of mysterious feeling in the soul is quite interesting. Once it's explained, it won't work. But if one understands why smoke must ultimately be drawn out from the mouth, and fly from the house to the outside of the window; why ripples rise on the water when the breeze blows; why stars twinkle; and why people are so fond of cigarettes – it's all the same. Understanding these things can reveal the secrets of smokers.

Actually, there are no secrets. All that's needed is a knowing smile and understanding.

Amateur Mailbox

Diploma and Unemployment 246

Recently, this column has received many letters from young students who have encountered difficulties in terms of qualifications regarding the current educational administration and graduation diplomas, and are requesting the editor to help them resolve these issues. This is an inevitable phenomenon in the transitional era of reforming education and administration, and it is necessary to discuss it. Now, let's first analyze the questions asked.

(1) Cannot find a job because of lacking a graduation diploma

(2) Without a graduation diploma, even if one has the same level of education and financial ability, one cannot go to accredited secondary or higher schools.

(3) Accredited universities and secondary schools refuse to allow students who have not passed the joint entrance examination to take the exam.

(4) Students of unaccredited missionary schools cannot go to accredited schools.

Let's talk about the first question first.

other people introduce you, it is very difficult. Many people with high qualifications and academic abilities are also encountering the difficulty of unemployment. This kind of qualification-limiting situation can show the seriousness of the unemployment panic and the public's desire to pay a low price and hire people with higher abilities. Therefore, this is really not a matter of diplomas or not, but how to solve the unemployment panic and make demand exceed supply.

We feel that these people without graduation diplomas do not need to worry too much, because although all agencies and shops, etc., specify the minimum qualifications when hiring personnel, they will never only want qualifications and diplomas, and not need people with real talent and practical knowledge to work for them! Therefore, as long as you have the ability, you can be attentive and work hard, you can always find the job you need and can handle.

As for positive remedial measures, the only option is to go to school to pursue a diploma. If qualifications and finances are also a problem, then you can go to a tutorial school. The certificate from this kind of school may be able to help a little.

The nature of the second, third, and fourth questions is similar. It is related to the entire education and administration issue. To talk about it, it is a long story. Due to space limitations, we can only talk about the attitude that students with unqualified qualifications should take during this transitional period of reforming education administration.

Now, many students are unable to go to school due to qualification restrictions, and often develop a sense of frustration and sadness. This is really wrong. You need to know that the purpose of going to school is to gain knowledge, not to get a diploma. Then where is not a place to learn? Your surroundings are really all knowledge that you can explore. Why must you study in this narrow school? And why feel frustrated because you cannot go to school?

Therefore, students of unaccredited schools and other students with unqualified qualifications, under this difficult situation, in addition to trying their best to transfer to accredited schools, when there is no other choice, they can only go to unaccredited schools or tutorial schools. It's still studying the same way. As long as you work hard and strive to improve, you will never be any different from accredited students. Because studying is entirely a personal matter. No matter how good the school is, if you do not have real ability, then even if you have a diploma, its effectiveness is limited!

Finally, the editor hopes that the education authorities will devise fundamental solutions to remedy these young people who have no access to education, such as re-holding identification exams for private school students, strictly investigating the contents of various unaccredited schools, forcing them to become accredited, and establishing specialized schools to accommodate these students with unqualified qualifications, etc.

Novel

Uncle's Braid (10) (4) 247

— Linghe

Hengfeng's business was very good, this was a very obvious fact. Although no one except old man Mao knew exactly how much money they made each day, it was quite impressive that they could sell two dou of soybeans' worth of tofu a day. In addition, old man Mao and his wife were both very amiable in business, and besides, there was only this one store in these hundred-odd villages, so every time old man Mao saw the spring couplets written for him by the schoolteacher posted on the storefront, ("The earth returns to spring, the four seasons are always flourishing"), ("The farmers are universally happy, the five grains are abundant"), plus the horizontal banner of ("Business is booming"), his chubby face could not help but smile. As for the schoolteacher, it could be seen from the sixteen words in the couplets that he was an extraordinary scholar, embedding the four characters of (Datian) (Hengfeng) in the middle. The village name and the store name were both inside, which was quite difficult. Although old man Mao was not a scholar, he still knew some characters himself. After some explanation by others, he understood these things very well.

Tonight, Gray Hen was once again drinking liquor by the counter, but this time it wasn't fennel beans to go with the liquor, but peanuts worth ten coins. Beside him, there were four people playing cards. In addition to the proprietress, there was also sixth grandfather, the tailor Xi Gou, and the barber Chang Yan, who lived in the village. In addition, Daoist priest (note) Jin Rong and the chicken castrator San Lantou were all watching the game. Boss Mao was leaning on the counter, smoking a water pipe. The kerosene lamp beside his hand, no matter how blackened the glass lamp shade was by the smoke, was much brighter than an oil lamp. That kind of light shone on his face, showing a kind of greyish-white color.

The air in the store was filled with the peaceful breathing of people. Obviously, the so-called Restoration or the Revolutionary Party and other major national events did not bring about significant changes among them. Although there were already two shaven-headed monks in the village, when everyone first heard about this news in the afternoon, they had discussed it excitedly. But by the evening, because most of the people were paying attention to the card game of twenty coins per dou, the win or loss of eighty coins for a dou of cards was indeed a large sum for them. So, words like ("A foreign devil") ("Two shaven heads") were not heard much now.

However, Gray Hen had never played cards in his life, so naturally, the card game of six or seven people could not arouse his interest at all. He was still quietly drinking his liquor and slowly peeling the peanuts. He occasionally stretched his head over the proprietress's shoulder to watch her play cards. The flame of the candle flickered and jumped, and it took a lot of effort for his eyes to see the cards clearly, so he thought that this "one wan, three cakes, six strings" kind of thing was ultimately meaningless. At the same time, lighting two red candles for the sake of playing cards would cost more than a hundred coins, which was too uneconomical.
